    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app',

My favorite season will always be season 1, but I loved the other two seasons and the bonus Season Zero,<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I have and I fell in love with it right away! My favorite season will always be season 1, but I loved the other two seasons and the bonus Season Zero, as well as the little extras that went along with it. I'm looking forward to the movie that they're making for it, as well. It's nothing like the book, but I think I enjoyed it so much because I went into it figuring it wouldn't be so I was able to view as its own thing that was inspired by an awesome book.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I liked it - Gothic castle in Styria, mix of authentic vampire folklore - Carmilla is not pale nor burn in the sun - and Gothic romanticism. Carmilla <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I liked it - Gothic castle in Styria, mix of authentic vampire folklore - Carmilla is not pale nor burn in the sun - and Gothic romanticism. Carmilla is gorgeous and has some effective dialogue. But it has zero action, lot of talk... so if you are bored by talky, actionless stories, you may not enjoy this. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/750816181?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer750816181" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10454463020016266331"><b>
  <u>Bloody relevant to read!</u>
</b><br/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>BEFORE DRACULA, THERE WAS...</u>
</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>But to die as lovers may - to die together, so that they may live together.</i>
</b><br/><br/>This is a very important book in historic sense, in the genre of vampire reading, due that it was published 25 years before than <i>Dracula</i>. <br/><br/>Also, it presented lesbian situations, easily one of the first open mentions of the topic in literature.<br/><br/>So, it was a pioneer book in two subjects: Vampires and Lesbian literature.<br/><br/>Some may wonder how it was possible to publi</span>
  <span id="freeText10454463020016266331" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>Bloody relevant to read!</u>
</b><br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>BEFORE DRACULA, THERE WAS...</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>But to die as lovers may - to die together, so that they may live together.</i>
</b><br /><br />This is a very important book in historic sense, in the genre of vampire reading, due that it was published 25 years before than <i>Dracula</i>. <br /><br />Also, it presented lesbian situations, easily one of the first open mentions of the topic in literature.<br /><br />So, it was a pioneer book in two subjects: Vampires and Lesbian literature.<br /><br />Some may wonder how it was possible to publish a book with lesbian issues in 1872.<br /><br />Joseph Sheridan Le Fanú was ingenious in that, since when he was asked about, he just replied that it wasn't a homosexual situation since Carmilla was a vampire and due that, it was a creature without sexual genre.<br /><br />Sneaky devil this Le Fanu!<br /><br />Of course, that was a trick by the author but it worked since the book didn't have any trouble to be published in those times when there was a extremely close-minded attitude.<br /><br />And certainly the importance of the book to the eventual sucess of Bram Stoker's novel was fundamental.<br /><br />Without <i>Carmilla</i> there weren't <i>Dracula</i> and due that maybe there weren't a vampire sub-genre in the horror books that now it's one of the strongest subjects in modern paranormal literature.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>BRITISH GOTHIC</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Nevertheless, life and death are mysterious states, and we know little of the resources of either.</i>
</b><br /><br />Le Fanú also was the father of the Gothic horror of Britain establishing the style of how that kind of literature would be written even on these days.<br /><br />Maybe the only trouble with <i>Carmilla</i> to be read by current readers is its form of mystery that it's impossible that anybody would pick nowadays this particular novel to read without the previous knowledge that Carmilla is a vampire, and due that, the reader felt like reading a mystery where one already knows the answer to the mystery.<br /><br />The clues to the real nature of Carmilla are elegant and stylish but too evident for any reader familiar with vampire-related similar books, movies, TV series, etc...<br /><br />It's clear that <i>Carmilla</i> started all and the reality is that anybody else copied <b>FROM</b> it, but sadly, in many case, readers find the book way after of being already too familiar with the general world of vampires, diminishing the shock that the book could ever do.<br /><br />However, it's still an important book in literature history.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10454463020016266331" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10937061322685821601">In many ways the antithesis of <i>Dracula</i>, and if Stoker's novel disappointed me with its clean-cut, heterosexual male-influenced dichotomies, than le Fanu's novella is the flipside of the coin: female-centric, homoerotic, ambiguous and enigmatic (and all in about a quarter of the length!). Here the vampire is not the withered, evil "Other" but the beautiful, sensuous stranger that is readily welcomed into home and heart, becoming the double for the protagonist, leading to a very different sense of</span>
  <span id="freeText10937061322685821601" style="display:none">In many ways the antithesis of <i>Dracula</i>, and if Stoker's novel disappointed me with its clean-cut, heterosexual male-influenced dichotomies, than le Fanu's novella is the flipside of the coin: female-centric, homoerotic, ambiguous and enigmatic (and all in about a quarter of the length!). Here the vampire is not the withered, evil "Other" but the beautiful, sensuous stranger that is readily welcomed into home and heart, becoming the double for the protagonist, leading to a very different sense of horror--the necessary destruction not of an enemy but a loved one, perhaps even the self. It's a really eerie, beguiling little novella, uncanny in a way that <i>Dracula</i> only is in brief flashes... <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_320127602" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer320127602" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5106970422746924248">Carmilla, J. Sheridan Le Fanu<br/>Carmilla is a Gothic novella by Joseph Sheridan Le Fanu and one of the early works of vampire fiction, predating Bram Stoker's Dracula (1897) by 26 years. First published as a serial in The Dark Blue (1871–72), the story is narrated by a young woman preyed upon by a female vampire named Carmilla, later revealed to be Mircalla, Countess Karnstein (Carmilla is an anagram of Mircalla). The story is often anthologized and has been adapted many times in film and other med</span>
  <span id="freeText5106970422746924248" style="display:none">Carmilla, J. Sheridan Le Fanu<br />Carmilla is a Gothic novella by Joseph Sheridan Le Fanu and one of the early works of vampire fiction, predating Bram Stoker's Dracula (1897) by 26 years. First published as a serial in The Dark Blue (1871–72), the story is narrated by a young woman preyed upon by a female vampire named Carmilla, later revealed to be Mircalla, Countess Karnstein (Carmilla is an anagram of Mircalla). The story is often anthologized and has been adapted many times in film and other media.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز بیست و چهارم ماه ژوئن سال 2008 میلادی به زبان اصلی<br />عنوان: کارمیلا؛ نویسنده: جوزف شریدان له فانو؛ برگردان: هامون جعفرنژاد؛ مشهد، بوتیمار، 1394، در 125 ص؛ شابک: 9786004040334؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان ایرلندی - سده 19 م<br /><br />کارمیلا نام یکی از نخستین شخصیت‌های خون آشام ادبیات است. این شخصیت، بر خلاف «دراکولا»، یک زن است، و البته جای یادآوری دارد، که رمان «دراکولا»، نوشته ی «برام استوکر»، پس از «کارمیلا» نوشته و منتشر شده است، بنابراین هستند کسانیکه میگویند: «استوکر در نوشتن دراکولا از لی فانو تاثیر گرفته است». «کارمیلا» اشراف زاده ای نفرین شده است، او به خون آشامی‌ اشتغال دارد. «کارمیلا» ظاهر یک دختر جوان زیبا را دارد، که زیبایی و معصومیتش، جذاب و گیراست. دندان‌های نیش او، نه به اندازه ای که خیلی مشهود باشند، اما تا حد مشخصی، تیز هستند، تا نیمه شب، بتواند آن‌ها را در سینه ی قربانی فرو برده، و از خونش تغذیه کند. «کارمیلا»، گاهی به طور ناگهانی، غیب میشود، و پس از مدتی، دوباره در محل غیب شدن خویش، دیده می‌شود. او با شنیدن حرف‌های مذهبی، یا سرودهای کلیسایی، رو ترش می‌کند، و محل را ترک می‌کند. «کارمیلا»، برای جذب قربانی، مدت‌ها زمان صرف می‌کند، تا به او نزدیک شود، و محبت بسیاری برای قربانی روا میدارد. نقل از متن کتاب: «در شبی مهتابی، پس از غروب کامل آفتاب، به بالای یکی از برج‌های کلیسا رفت، و از پنجره‌ اش قبرستان را زیر نظر گرفت. لباسی از جنس کتان را، که پیشتر تا کرده بود، در کنار قبر قرار داد، و به سمت دهکده‌ ای به راه افتاد، تا طاعونش را بر سر اهالی آن فرود آورد؛ ...»، پایان نقل از متن کتاب. ا. شربیانی</span>
  <a data-text-id="5106970422746924248" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1856176901" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1856176901" />
    <a title="Graeme Rodaughan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56397934-graeme-rodaughan"><img alt="Graeme Rodaughan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464911366p2/56397934.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1856176901?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Graeme Rodaughan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Graeme Rodaughan" href="/user/show/56397934-graeme-rodaughan">Graeme Rodaughan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone who loves a languid, creepy, and spooky story.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56397934-graeme-rodaughan?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56397934-graeme-rodaughan?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56397934-graeme-rodaughan?shelf=gets-under-your-skin">gets-under-your-skin</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1856176901" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16440072775072315477"><b>Horror Reader Shocker! Spooky Vampire Leaves Wannabe Author Prostrated!: "What the FRACK!!! I can't get her out of my head!" - Vampire Guild Weekly</b><br/><br/>After reading this book, I am left frustrated and oddly underwhelmed, and yet there is an undeniable and dare I say it <b>'uncanny,'</b> power to this story which is a mystery to me.<br/><br/>The smartest character in the story is the antagonist (who is not that smart), who proceeds to charm and bamboozle an array of protagonists who are all very nice, and not the lea</span>
  <span id="freeText16440072775072315477" style="display:none"><b>Horror Reader Shocker! Spooky Vampire Leaves Wannabe Author Prostrated!: "What the FRACK!!! I can't get her out of my head!" - Vampire Guild Weekly</b><br /><br />After reading this book, I am left frustrated and oddly underwhelmed, and yet there is an undeniable and dare I say it <b>'uncanny,'</b> power to this story which is a mystery to me.<br /><br />The smartest character in the story is the antagonist (who is not that smart), who proceeds to charm and bamboozle an array of protagonists who are all very nice, and not the least given to suspicion of others.<br /><br />There are multiple events where the fact that Carmilla is a vampire is hinted at with growing strength, up to and including the discovery of a perfect portrait painted in the dim past. Le Fanu doesn't quite get to the point of hanging a sign, written in fresh blood around Carmilla's neck proclaiming, "I am a vampire, and I am here to kill you." But he gets close.<br /><br />With the characters stumbling about in their ignorance as the Vampire runs rings around them - I was left imagining shooting fish in a barrel. I found myself thinking what if a terrible blizzard arrived that shut up the Schloss for 3 days (and especially 3 nights). Leaving Carmilla alone with only the hero - Laura (our narrator), her father, the governess, and the other staff without any hope of escape. As the death toll mounted, the presence of a vampire would quickly become obvious. Laura would then be confronted with a need to make a decision of consequence and take irrevocable action. Something she really doesn't get much of a chance to do.<br /><br />Passive characters, especially if the narrator are frustrating.<br /><br />On the plus side, the author has made an excellent stab at establishing the vampire genre. He has also provided a clever subplot of lesbian love. Neither would have been easy to do in his day and age.<br /><br />Also the description of the actual vampire attacks is genuinely spooky and admirable writing.<br /><br />While this book failed to excite me with it's general lack of pace and suspense, It has deep qualities that many would appreciate. Especially those with a taste for "Creeping Horror."<br /><br /><b>On a decidedly UNCANNY personal note.</b> ... I had a dream, an incredibly VIVID dream, while reading this novel where I was visited by a magnetic, alluring, dark-haired female vampire and I willing offered my arm to her. Something that I have never done before in a dream. What was also noteworthy was the experience of an abiding personal intimacy that accompanied the act of freely giving blood to sustain another.<br /><br /><blockquote>The sultry summer evening had barely given way to the night. I had left the bedroom doors open to the balcony to allow a light breeze to circulate. I lay back on the bed, tossing and turning, unable to sleep. The house belonged to me, I was its sole occupant, but the loneliness of this house weighed heavily - it was not a home.<br /><br />Moonlight cut through the room, then it vanished for an instant. A momentary shadow flitting through the doorway, entering my bedroom and filling it with a pervasive sense of possession - the room was no longer mine.<br /><br />My heart thudded in my chest. I sat up suddenly, pressing backward against the headboard. There was someone in the room, the feeling of <i>Her</i> presence was overwhelming, but I couldn't see anyone - there was no one there.<br /><br />The shadows thickened at the end of my bed. I stared, frozen where I sat, as the shadows coalesced into the ethereal shape of a young woman. She wore a light diaphanous gown. Her hair was lustrous black, her skin pale like marble, her eyes were large and dark, her lips red, full and slightly curved in a coy smile.<br /><br />Her form solidified. A faint perfume filled the air. She seemed deeply familiar, and yet, I had never seen her before - at least I had no memory of ever meeting her and I'm sure I would not have forgotten.<br /><br />She moved to her right, floating, lithe, serene. She was majestic and mesmerizing - power beyond words was bound up in her gaze. Her eyes glittered like black diamonds, brilliant and hard. I couldn't tear my eyes away from them even if I tried.<br /><br />She sat down beside me, gently picking up my left arm with her cool hands. She turned it over, palm up. I didn't resist - I didn't want to. I lifted my arm up and she lent forward. <br /><br />A bell rang in the distance, a muffled warning - ignored and discarded in the face of her needs. Needs I was a willing servant to.<br /><br />Moonlight gleamed on her ivory fangs. She leaned further in, first kissing, then licking - finally biting. A single drop of blood fell off my wrist, dark against the white bed sheet. She murmured in delight, my heart beat hard in my chest, but I stayed still - unwilling to disturb her feast.<br /><br />Everything was for her...<br /><br />(inspired by my dream while reading this book...)</blockquote><br /><br /><b>I am left wondering just how deep this story can creep into you when you read it?</b><br /><br /><b>Strongly Recommended. 5 'Spooky Vampire Kisses Beneath the Moonlight Stars.'</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="16440072775072315477" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1569321808" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1569321808" />
    <a title="Fabian {Councillor}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40792319-fabian-councillor"><img alt="Fabian {Councillor}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599133151p2/40792319.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1569321808?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fabian {Councillor}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fabian {Councillor}" href="/user/show/40792319-fabian-councillor">Fabian {Councillor}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of the horror genre</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=read-in-one-sitting">read-in-one-sitting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=paranormal-fantasy">paranormal-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=gothic">gothic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=year-1870s">year-1870s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1569321808" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10232749302227816632">With <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17245.Dracula' title='Dracula by Bram Stoker' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dracula</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5297.The_Picture_of_Dorian_Gray' title='The Picture of Dorian Gray by Oscar Wilde' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Picture of Dorian Gray</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/51496.The_Strange_Case_of_Dr__Jekyll_and_Mr__Hyde' title='The Strange Case of Dr. Jekyll and Mr. Hyde by Robert Louis Stevenson' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Strange Case of Dr. Jekyll and Mr. Hyde</a>, some of the most famously recognized horror stories of the nineteenth century have been created, yet only few people seem to know this little story which may have been the ultimate inspiration for Bram Stoker to write his popular novel <i>Dracula</i>. <i>Carmilla</i> is an early vampire story, laying the foundation of a genre which would see many other vampire tales in the upcoming years, until the development recently c</span>
  <span id="freeText10232749302227816632" style="display:none">With <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17245.Dracula" title="Dracula by Bram Stoker" rel="nofollow noopener">Dracula</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5297.The_Picture_of_Dorian_Gray" title="The Picture of Dorian Gray by Oscar Wilde" rel="nofollow noopener">The Picture of Dorian Gray</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/51496.The_Strange_Case_of_Dr__Jekyll_and_Mr__Hyde" title="The Strange Case of Dr. Jekyll and Mr. Hyde by Robert Louis Stevenson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Strange Case of Dr. Jekyll and Mr. Hyde</a>, some of the most famously recognized horror stories of the nineteenth century have been created, yet only few people seem to know this little story which may have been the ultimate inspiration for Bram Stoker to write his popular novel <i>Dracula</i>. <i>Carmilla</i> is an early vampire story, laying the foundation of a genre which would see many other vampire tales in the upcoming years, until the development recently culminated in the seemingly perfect picture of the attractive, charming and oh so sexy vampire. Le Fanu's tale, only 100 pages long and perfect to read as a two-hour-long distraction during a Sunday afternoon, may seem unoriginal and inferior compared to the huge stories listed in the beginning ... but looking closer at this, it might be easier to realize that "Carmilla" is much more than that.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459701404i/18645006._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Set in a gothic atmosphere surrounding the Austrian castle home of the first-person narrator, eighteen-year-old Laura, and her father, <i>Carmilla</i> tells the story of a young lady who comes to visit them under mysterious circumstances, with death and nightmares falling over the inhabitants of the castle and the vicinity soon. Not only does this premise introduce an interesting development - seldomly could it have been possible to find a female character in such astonishing circumstances in the 19th century - but also does the author prove himself to be far ahead of his time, including several homosexual allusions and thus being one of the first authors of his time to do so. Most of the events in this novel are implied rather than accurately explained, which strengthens the chilling atmosphere and makes up for a thrilling reading experience.<br><br>Le Fanu's writing is anything but tiresome. While the gothic influence can easily be recognized in the novel, it feels like the writing could also have originated in modern days. Slowly does the horror creep inside the pages, and short chapters as well as fast-paced scenes help the reader to hasten through those pages. Apart from the dumb and rather annoying protagonist and the casual, perhaps even lazy characterization, <i>Carmilla</i> is a fascinating tale which should be read by everyone interested in the gothic horror genre and, generally, by horror readers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10232749302227816632" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3216916678" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3216916678" />
    <a title="Alex" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3144945-alex"><img alt="Alex" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594856152p2/3144945.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3216916678?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex" href="/user/show/3144945-alex">Alex</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3144945-alex?shelf=2020">2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3216916678" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5277345714582188118">Vampires are gay. They've always been gay. Twilight was literally the first vampire story that wasn't gay. (Unless it was? I don't know, I didn't read it.) Dracula was our pioneering gay male vampire story. <i>Carmilla</i>, which predates it by some twenty years, is our pioneering lesbian one.<br/><br/>The authors themselves are not always gay. Bram Stoker was, of course - gayer than a guy who knows how to change the sheets on his bed - but Sheridan Le Fanu, the popular and terrific 1800s Gothic writer responsib</span>
  <span id="freeText5277345714582188118" style="display:none">Vampires are gay. They've always been gay. Twilight was literally the first vampire story that wasn't gay. (Unless it was? I don't know, I didn't read it.) Dracula was our pioneering gay male vampire story. <i>Carmilla</i>, which predates it by some twenty years, is our pioneering lesbian one.<br><br>The authors themselves are not always gay. Bram Stoker was, of course - gayer than a guy who knows how to change the sheets on his bed - but Sheridan Le Fanu, the popular and terrific 1800s Gothic writer responsible for <i>Carmilla</i>, seems like a cousin-fucker but a straight one. And this is, if we're being honest, lesbians more of the "nightgowns and swooning" variety than the "roommates who enjoy pants" variety. ("Roommates who enjoy pants" is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25104465-tipping-the-velvet?from_search=true&amp;qid=IE4AyGu32g&amp;rank=1" title="well obviously I'm not going to not bring up Tipping the Velvet" rel="nofollow noopener">what they called them</a> back then.) So this is lesbians by way of the male gaze, and with quite a lot of Daddy Issues mixed in. "My hot daughter's hot friend keeps flouncing about in nightgowns," is one way you could describe the plot. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">["Eventually I had to murder her naked body" is how these things end - they find her floating naked in a coffin full of blood, by the way, that's amazing - and  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I mean we've all <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-O3cU3dODjo" title="The trailer for this excellent movie" rel="nofollow noopener">seen Poison Ivy,</a> right? Do a shot for every time you see the word "languid". <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1584647672i/29132942._SX540_.jpg" alt="poison-ivy" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Ch-ch-ch-ch-ch-ch-ch-ch-cherry bomb</i><br><br>The hot daughter and her single father live in an old castle ("schloss" is now a word you know) in the middle of nowhere, because of course they do, and a total stranger driving by leaves her hot teenage daughter with them for a few months because she fainted. That's the plot. They set the nubile stranger up in the bedroom that has a tapestry of Cleopatra holding poisonous asps to her bosom, and can I tell you how much I love imagining that decorating decision. "What if we make this room the Dead Naked Lady Room?" Cool. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1584647672i/29132939._SY540_.jpg" alt="cloepatar" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Cleopatra And The Asp by Girolamo di Benvenuto, 1500ish</i><br><br>Townspeople are dying, as they do. Carmilla's door is locked from the inside at night. She comes down late in the morning. "My strange and beautiful companion," says daughter Laura,<blockquote>
<br>"would take my hand and hold it with a fond pressure, renewed again and again; blushing softly, gazing in my face with languid and burning eyes, and breathing so fast that her dress rose and fell with the tumultuous respiration. It was like the ardor of a lover; it embarrassed me; it was hateful and yet over-powering; and with gloating eyes she drew me to her, and her hot lips traveled along my cheek in kisses; and she would whisper, almost in sobs, "You are mine, you shall be mine, you and I are one for ever." Then she had thrown herself back in her chair, with her small hands over her eyes, leaving me trembling.</blockquote><br>Do a shot for "languid." And should this be taken seriously? Is it literature? Is it great vampire literature? Are vampires inherently silly? <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1584647672i/29132940._SY540_.png" alt="sheridan" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Sheridan Le Fanu: would you bang, yes or no</i><br><br>Vampire books are mostly gay and always about sex. Dangerous visitors to your bedroom at night! Certainly Le Fanu intended <i>Carmilla</i> to be hot, and if Stoker didn't <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/217034147" title="My review of Dracula" rel="nofollow noopener">intend Dracula to be</a> it was only because he was so far back in the closet that he ended up in Narnia. But of course vampires are predators, as well, so there's an element of "these depraved homosexuals," right? "So hot! But so dangerous! But so hot!" I hope that in these enlightened times we're slightly less panicky about the vast spectrum of our sexual desire. But sex is still dangerous, and it seems to me like a serious concern. Books about sex are worthy. And what other books, particularly in the stodgy 1800s, were about sex? If you didn't smuggle it into a vampire book, where else would you find it? Henry James certainly <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2508609802" title="My review of Daisy Miller" rel="nofollow noopener">wasn't helping anyone.</a><br><br>What I love about this particular edition of <i>Carmilla</i> by Lanternfish Press is that they've convinced the mighty Carmen Maria Machado, a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2234188654" title="My review of Her Body and Other Parties" rel="nofollow noopener">Gothic lover herself,</a> to write an intro where she says all the quiet parts out loud. Machado first of all insists that the entire thing is true, producing historical documents like a righteous gay <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/145560209" title="not to say there hasn't been some speculation about Borges" rel="nofollow noopener">Borges,</a> and then further accuses Le Fanu of straightwashing the story. It's not gay <i>enough,</i> she says. The true story would have been about about "a young woman’s sexual awakening; the senseless slaughter of her supposed defiler.” Machado points out that gay passion is often read as murderous (hello, <a href="" title="My review of The Talented Mr Ripley" rel="nofollow noopener">Patricia Highsmith</a>), while making a driveby suggestion that the infamous Countess Bathory (of Blood) was bathing less in virgin blood than in their vaginas. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1584647672i/29132938._SY540_.jpg" alt="Elizabeth-Bathory-Portrait" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Countess Bathory, one kind of scissor fighter or another</i><br><br>Machado continues,<br><blockquote>The act of interacting with text - that is to say, of reading - is that of inserting ones self into what is static and unchanging sounds that it might pump with fresh blood. Having read this introduction, I hope you will enter into Carmilla thusly, using your fingertips and mouth and mind to locate ...what exists below: the erotic relationship of two high-strung and lonely young women.</blockquote><br>This whole thing is, of course, a meta joke about our modern hobby of declaring old books gay. Carmen Maria Machado is fingerbanging <i>Carmilla.</i> But under that, there's something serious going on, right? This is a declaration of our <i>right</i> to interpret old books however we want to. The book is as gay as we say it is, she suggests. The words on the page are, of course, static and unchanging. But when we go down on them, we open them up and find new meanings hidden inside, and those are not only valid but crucial to the survival of the book. If there's nothing hidden in it, it doesn't matter. "Girls are caterpillars when they live in the world," says Carmilla, <blockquote>
<br>to be finally butterflies when the summer comes; but in the meantime there are grubs and larvae, don't you see - each with their peculiar propensities, necessities and structures.</blockquote><br>A book can be lurid and great at the same time, and <i>Carmilla</i> certainly is both. I love every preposterous sentence of it. Look at this indelible scene where the vampire appears at Laura's bed, her nightgown drenched in blood. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1584647672i/29132941._SY540_.jpg" alt="IMG-6864" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Illustration from the Lanternfish edition</i><br><br>The image was echoed by Stephen King 100 years later in Carrie, another great novel about the terror of feminine sexuality. It's spectacular, and <i>Carmilla</i> is still a gripping and unnerving book. It has plenty of secrets and peculiar propensities left for our probing fingertips.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="5277345714582188118" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_18368275" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/18368275" />
    <a title="Werner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/903390-werner"><img alt="Werner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1216337931p2/903390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/18368275?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Werner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Werner" href="/user/show/903390-werner">Werner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Any fan of vampire fiction, or of supernatural fiction in general</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/903390-werner?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/903390-werner?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/903390-werner?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/903390-werner?shelf=supernatural-fiction">supernatural-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18368275" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5193985852987277215">Note, Oct. 1, 2012: I just modified this review slightly to incorporate a changed perspective I came to as a result of a discussion in one of my groups.<br/><br/>This book is one of the best treatments of the vampire theme I have read (admittedly, I haven't read very many --even counting the ones I didn't like enough to finish!). While the author's diction is Victorian, the book is a short, quick read (unlike the massive tomes that some 19th-century novels are), so it shouldn't be daunting even for reader</span>
  <span id="freeText5193985852987277215" style="display:none">Note, Oct. 1, 2012: I just modified this review slightly to incorporate a changed perspective I came to as a result of a discussion in one of my groups.<br /><br />This book is one of the best treatments of the vampire theme I have read (admittedly, I haven't read very many --even counting the ones I didn't like enough to finish!). While the author's diction is Victorian, the book is a short, quick read (unlike the massive tomes that some 19th-century novels are), so it shouldn't be daunting even for readers who have a problem with old-fashioned prose. Unlike John Polidori's Lord Ruthven and the title character of <i>Varney the Vampire</i>, LeFanu's vampire is female. He concentrates on psychological horror rather than on blood and gore, and does not try to eroticize the vampire's activities. (Carmilla definitely does use language in places that suggests that she demands an attachment from her female victims that borders on romantic love, which gives her attitude what today would be called a "lesbian" undercurrent; but we can also fairly say that even though she wants strong female attachment, it's not genitally sexual in nature.) The atmosphere of menace and suspense easily evokes the reader's concerned attention.<br /><br />One of the characters here is an eccentric scholar with knowledge of vampire lore (a kind of adumbration of Stoker's Van Helsing). Also, Le Fanu indicates the hostility between the vampire and Christian faith (his vampire, of course, is in the classic mold --an instinctively evil embodiment of appetite and cunning malevolence, rather than a person with a moral free will and an individual personality, like many modern fictional vampires), but doesn't develop this theme as fully as Stoker does in <i>Dracula</i>. For a reader who enjoys seeing fiction in its historical and literary context, it's fascinating to see the way elements whose seeds are planted by the earlier writer are more fully developed by the later one!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5193985852987277215" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1183569870" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1183569870" />
    <a title="Candi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3639005-candi"><img alt="Candi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585187464p2/3639005.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1183569870?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candi" href="/user/show/3639005-candi">Candi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24184721-carmilla">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3639005-candi?shelf=horror-creepy">horror-creepy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3639005-candi?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3639005-candi?shelf=classics-shelf">classics-shelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1183569870" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18353856724307499887"><i>"The amphibious existence of the vampire is sustained by daily renewed slumber in the grave. Its horrible lust for living blood supplies the vigor of its waking existence. The vampire is prone to be fascinated with an engrossing vehemence, resembling the passion of love, by particular persons… It will never desist until it has satiated its passion, and drained the very life of its coveted victim."</i><br/><br/>This description of a vampire is not anything new and surprising to anyone that has an interest in v</span>
  <span id="freeText18353856724307499887" style="display:none"><i>"The amphibious existence of the vampire is sustained by daily renewed slumber in the grave. Its horrible lust for living blood supplies the vigor of its waking existence. The vampire is prone to be fascinated with an engrossing vehemence, resembling the passion of love, by particular persons… It will never desist until it has satiated its passion, and drained the very life of its coveted victim."</i><br /><br />This description of a vampire is not anything new and surprising to anyone that has an interest in vampire lore, but what is amazing about these words are that they were written prior to Bram Stoker's <b>Dracula</b>. Le Fanu's <b>Carmilla</b> is a short but impressive tale of a female vampire which I found to be wonderfully gothic and appropriately spine-chilling. <br /><br />Rumors of a strange sickness circulating the area of Styria in Austria come to the attention of a young lady, Laura, and her father at their secluded castle. Shortly thereafter, these two find themselves with a very mysterious guest following a carriage accident just outside the confines of their palatial home. Laura, our narrator, reflects upon the face of this guest as being one that appeared to her in a very vivid and disturbing childhood dream. Despite this fact, the lonely Laura becomes quickly attached to her newly found companion, Carmilla. <i>"I did feel drawn towards her but there was also something of repulsion. In this ambiguous feeling, however, the sense of attraction immensely prevailed… she was so beautiful and indescribably engaging."</i> As time goes on, Laura is not able to glean any background information from this extraordinary guest. Where did she come from? To which place was she headed? And, why did her mother leave her in the hands of strangers whilst hastening on to some secretive destination? <br /> <br />The suspense of the novel increases as Laura becomes once again plagued by nightmares and strange occurrences. A gradual decline in Laura's health and sinister reports shared by a respected friend in the neighborhood prompt Laura's father to obtain answers and spur him to action. The events that follow are dramatic and exciting. <br /><br />I found the plot of this book to be a bit uneven at times. It also seemed a bit too short - I think the story could have been developed a bit further. Overall though, there was great atmosphere, and it was fun and well-done for an early vampire story. It would translate really well into an excellent movie! 3.5 stars<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18353856724307499887" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<span id="freeTextContainer15678055205017730983">Hellow,<br/>Aren't the books that we like the most, the harder to review?<br/>Carmilla by Joseph Sheridan Le Fanu became one of my favourite book of all time, it spoke to my soul through words of darkness, each sentence was like sweet melancholic music echoing and engraving in me.<br/>Sentences like “Girls are caterpillars while they live in the world, to be finally butterflies when the summer comes; but in the meantime there are grubs and larvae, don't you see - each with their peculiar propensities, necessit</span>
  <span id="freeText15678055205017730983" style="display:none">Hellow,<br />Aren't the books that we like the most, the harder to review?<br />Carmilla by Joseph Sheridan Le Fanu became one of my favourite book of all time, it spoke to my soul through words of darkness, each sentence was like sweet melancholic music echoing and engraving in me.<br />Sentences like “Girls are caterpillars while they live in the world, to be finally butterflies when the summer comes; but in the meantime there are grubs and larvae, don't you see - each with their peculiar propensities, necessities and structure.” will never leave me be anymore.<br />It was short and like some classics the end was a bit rushed but the away it was written compensates every bit of hastiness on get in to the end.<br />Read it for the poetry on the words, when it comes to authors like Le Fanu, you have to see the writing as the experience, more even that the plot itself. Read it in a languish way,absorbing the luxurious sentences and get lost on the beauty of it.<br /><br />Regards.<br />Yours Sincerely,<br />SkeletonOrchid</span>

<div id="review_3065454510" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

<span id="freeTextContainer8425049156393551794">4 Stars for Carmilla: A Vampire Tale (audiobook) by J Sheridan Le Fanu read by Megan Follows. This is a very early gothic vampire tale. It was written 26 years before Bram Stoker wrote Dracula. It’s a rather short but very poetic story. I find it interesting to see how this mythology got its start. This was a great audiobook...5</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2159680601" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2159680601" />
    <a title="Apatt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2457095-apatt"><img alt="Apatt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349239948p2/2457095.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2159680601?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Apatt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Apatt" href="/user/show/2457095-apatt">Apatt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2457095-apatt?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2457095-apatt?shelf=classics">classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2159680601" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16015590177895535939"><i>“I am sure, Carmilla, you have been in love; that there is, at this moment, an affair of the heart going on."<br/><br/>"I have been in love with no one, and never shall," she whispered, "unless it should be with you."<br/><br/>How beautiful she looked in the moonlight!”</i><br/><br/>Very <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7577.Anne_Rice' title='Anne Rice' rel='nofollow noopener'> Anne Rice</a>, except that <i>Carmilla</i> predates Rice’s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43763.Interview_with_the_Vampire__The_Vampire_Chronicles___1_' title='Interview with the Vampire (The Vampire Chronicles, #1) by Anne Rice' rel='nofollow noopener'> Interview with the Vampire</a> by about a century, so Joseph Sheridan Le Fanu did the "sexy vampire" thing first. He did it even before <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6988.Bram_Stoker' title='Bram Stoker' rel='nofollow noopener'> Bram Stoker</a> unleashed <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17245.Dracula' title='Dracula by Bram Stoker' rel='nofollow noopener'> Dracula</a> on the world. <i>Carmilla</i> is one o</span>
  <span id="freeText16015590177895535939" style="display:none"><i>“I am sure, Carmilla, you have been in love; that there is, at this moment, an affair of the heart going on."<br><br>"I have been in love with no one, and never shall," she whispered, "unless it should be with you."<br><br>How beautiful she looked in the moonlight!”</i><br><br>Very <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7577.Anne_Rice" title="Anne Rice" rel="nofollow noopener"> Anne Rice</a>, except that <i>Carmilla</i> predates Rice’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43763.Interview_with_the_Vampire__The_Vampire_Chronicles___1_" title="Interview with the Vampire (The Vampire Chronicles, #1) by Anne Rice" rel="nofollow noopener"> Interview with the Vampire</a> by about a century, so Joseph Sheridan Le Fanu did the "sexy vampire" thing first. He did it even before <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6988.Bram_Stoker" title="Bram Stoker" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bram Stoker</a> unleashed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17245.Dracula" title="Dracula by Bram Stoker" rel="nofollow noopener"> Dracula</a> on the world. <i>Carmilla</i> is one of the earliest work of vampire fiction, apparently not <i>the</i>, I have no idea whose story has that honor (Google is your friend!).<br><br><a href="https://www.amazon.com.au/Carmilla/dp/B01BDAX8H2" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1508596568i/24233162._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="394" alt="audiobook" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </a><br>First published in 1871 <i>Carmilla</i> tells the story of Laura, a young woman living with her father in a “schloss” (castle) in Styria. One day a carriage transporting a lady and her daughter has an accident outside the castle, the daughter, Carmilla, is a little injured and cannot continue the journey with her mother. Laura’s father, nice fellow that he is, offers to take care of the lady’s daughter while the lady takes care of her business. The two girls (age not mentioned, but Laura is probably about 16-18 years old, Carmilla <i>looks</i> the same age) quickly become BFFs. Laura finds Carmilla to be great company, very pretty, enigmatic and a bit weird. A few days after their association Laura’s health begins to fail, she wakes up feeling more and more anemic every day. She has no idea why but, being a bit of a fool, tries to hide the condition from her father. We, of course, realize the truth immediately, Carmilla, her new BFF has been making happy meals out of her. Though she seems nice, she sucks.<br><br>The characterization of the eponymous Carmilla is quite well done, even when she is passing herself off as a girl she is creepy and charismatic. I can not say the same for the other characters, they are just there to serve the plot. Laura is too ineffectual to be of any interest and I am surprised Carmilla herself does not feel anemic from consuming her sappy blood. There is a mildly erotic angle to the story, which later authors like Anne Rice refined to an art form.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1508596568i/24233165.jpg" width="350" height="457" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>From <a href="http://www.victoriangothic.org/before-dracula-there-was-carmilla/" rel="nofollow noopener">Victorean Gothic's article</a><br><br><i>Carmilla</i> has a disadvantage often experienced by early practitioners of a new genre of fiction, the writers who followed refined the basic idea and did it much better. So Bram Stoker, Stephen King, Richard Matheson, GRRM, Anne Rice etc. basically wrote much better, more frightening and thrilling vampire stories. <i>Carmilla</i> is not at all bad, the early part of the novella creeped me out a little bit. Unfortunately, as the narrative progresses it seems to run out of steam, and the final encounter with Carmilla feels oddly flat and matter of fact. Still, the novella is too short to outstay its welcome and I kind of enjoyed it; not exactly a ringing endorsement, but it is in the public domain so you may as well give it a shot!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1508596568i/24233161._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="309" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>“Pardon me miss, do you happen to have a knife sharpener.... Ooer missus!”<br><br><b>Notes:</b><br>• The <a href="https://librivox.org/carmilla-by-sheridan-lefanu/" rel="nofollow noopener">free Librivox audiobook version</a> I listened to is read by the excellent Elizabeth Klett.<br>• There are several film adaptations of this book, but the most well known is probably <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0066518/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Vampire Lovers (1970)</a><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1508596568i/24233163.jpg" alt="bat line" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Quotes:</b><br><i>“Now the truth is, I felt rather unaccountably towards the beautiful stranger. I did feel, as she said, "drawn towards her," but there was also something of repulsion. In this ambiguous feeling, however, the sense of attraction immensely prevailed. She interested and won me; she was so beautiful and so indescribably engaging.”<br><br>“Shy and strange was the look with which she quickly hid her face in my neck and hair, with tumultuous sighs, that seemed almost to sob, and pressed in mine a hand that trembled.”<br><br>“Her soft cheek was glowing against mine. "Darling, darling," she murmured, "I live in you; and you would die for me, I love you so.”<br><br>“She and I talked a great deal, and very animated she was; and the remainder of that evening passed without any recurrence of what I called her infatuations. I mean her crazy talk and looks, which embarrassed, and even frightened me.”<br><br>“I saw a solemn, but very pretty face looking at me from the side of the bed. It was that of a young lady who was kneeling, with her hands under the coverlet. I looked at her with a kind of pleased wonder, and ceased whimpering. She caressed me with her hands, and lay down beside me on the bed, and drew me towards her, smiling; I felt immediately delightfully soothed, and fell asleep again. I was wakened by a sensation as if two needles ran into my breast very deep at the same moment, and I cried loudly. The lady started back, with her eyes fixed on me, and then slipped down upon the floor, and, as I thought, hid herself under the bed.”</i><br><br><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=FmkHqUwa4zg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1508596568i/24233164.jpg" alt="Halestorm" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/601865?chapter=1" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1507108616i/24082028.jpg" alt="Halloween Reads Fest 2017" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16015590177895535939" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2259003749" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2259003749" />
    <a title="Michael Sorbello" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4307906-michael-sorbello"><img alt="Michael Sorbello" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521124600p2/4307906.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2259003749?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Sorbello" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Sorbello" href="/user/show/4307906-michael-sorbello">Michael Sorbello</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780978454357" href="/book/show/17130812-carmilla">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4307906-michael-sorbello?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4307906-michael-sorbello?shelf=book-reviews">book-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2259003749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5064380523746965924">I loved Carmilla as a character. She truly was the original Dracula, leaving Bram Stoker with plenty of inspiration to craft his gothic classic. Carmilla is charming and cruel, broken and detached. A delightfully scary and haughty lady. The book was revolutionary in many ways, introducing the world to the first-known female vampire in the starring role of a novella, breaking the rules of the puritan society it was written in by exploring female sexuality and homoeroticism (in a similar fashion a</span>
  <span id="freeText5064380523746965924" style="display:none">I loved Carmilla as a character. She truly was the original Dracula, leaving Bram Stoker with plenty of inspiration to craft his gothic classic. Carmilla is charming and cruel, broken and detached. A delightfully scary and haughty lady. The book was revolutionary in many ways, introducing the world to the first-known female vampire in the starring role of a novella, breaking the rules of the puritan society it was written in by exploring female sexuality and homoeroticism (in a similar fashion as Oscar Wilde's Dorian Gray,) and combining horror with various other genres such as gothic fiction, paranormal romance, political drama and psychological ghost stories. <br /><br />Carmilla transforms the naive and innocent girl Laura into a woman through her signs of genuine affection and malicious manipulation. Preying upon and messing around with women that have connections to nobility has a price however, and this eventually leads to Carmilla getting caught red handed. Even after Carmilla is gone, she leaves a lasting impression on Laura, depicting the tragic symptoms of trauma-induced heartbreak upon having a sort of spiritual awakening and being made aware of the darker side of the world.<br /><br />***<br /><br />My Social Media<br /><br />My Instagram Account: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.instagram.com/michael_sorbello/">https://www.instagram.com/michael_sor...</a><br /><br />My Wattpad Account: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.wattpad.com/user/Michael-Sorbello">https://www.wattpad.com/user/Michael-...</a><br /><br />My YouTube Channel: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCPPs1eOzsOqcz5ey5JjGSbg">https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCPPs...</a><br /><br />My Twitter Account: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twitter.com/SorbelloHorror">https://twitter.com/SorbelloHorror</a><br /><br />My Facebook Account: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/michael.sorbello.104">https://www.facebook.com/michael.sorb...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5064380523746965924" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9709228932064077646">Such a classic, old school, vampire novel.<br/><br/>The unsuspecting hosts, the beautiful and mysterious guest. The strange behaviours of the beloved guest.<br/><br/>It just builds the suspense so brilliantly, and part of the fun is in seeing how these rational people deal with the irrational.<br/><br/>This one was interesting because the vampire is a girl very similar to her victim, and there is the element of friendship (and courtship?) that makes things so much more sinister</span>
  <span id="freeText9709228932064077646" style="display:none">Such a classic, old school, vampire novel.<br /><br />The unsuspecting hosts, the beautiful and mysterious guest. The girl who begins to grow wearier day by day. The strange behaviours of the beloved guest.<br /><br />It just builds the suspense so brilliantly, and part of the fun is in seeing how these rational people deal with the irrational.<br /><br />This one was interesting because the vampire is a girl very similar to her victim, and there is the element of friendship (and courtship?) that makes things so much more sinister. Every time Carmilla got handsy it gave me chills.<br /><br />A great little horror story for Halloween! </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/5858203-michelle">Michelle</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3050582637" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14795471155478208759">This book was published in 1872 and is said to be the book that later inspired Dracula, it was brought to my attention by a fellow book dragon Salema and I couldn't wait to read it.<br/><br/>It's a short novella at 108 pages and is available as a free download so if you're into your vampires get downloading! <br/><br/>I read this in one sitting, it's so readable for a book written so long ago and I must say I enjoyed it. I'm coming to realise that I do enjoy a book where the narration is directed at the reader, it </span>
  <span id="freeText14795471155478208759" style="display:none">This book was published in 1872 and is said to be the book that later inspired Dracula, it was brought to my attention by a fellow book dragon Salema and I couldn't wait to read it.<br /><br />It's a short novella at 108 pages and is available as a free download so if you're into your vampires get downloading! <br /><br />I read this in one sitting, it's so readable for a book written so long ago and I must say I enjoyed it. I'm coming to realise that I do enjoy a book where the narration is directed at the reader, it makes me feel a part of the cast and really improves the atmosphere the author is creating. <br /><br />This isnt the best vampire book out there but as one of the earliest vampire novellas and one that features female / female attractions I do feel this is worth a read, especially as it's so short and of course free!<br /><br />As with many classics I rate this three stars, its readable, its aged well but it didnt blow me away.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9380257318281659514">Update: currently revisiting this wonderful novella with the fine folks at the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/108-horror-aficionados' rel='nofollow noopener'> Horror Aficionados</a> group who have given me the the opportunity to read and discuss this and many other fine books.<br/><br/><br/>Predating Dracula by 26 years, Le Fanu's novella is a classic vampire tale that gets a lot less attention than it should. It is loaded with Gothic atmosphere and also introduces a lesbian vampire theme that, while appropriately circumspect, is unmistakable and something that I never would have expected in</span>
  <span id="freeText9380257318281659514" style="display:none">Update: currently revisiting this wonderful novella with the fine folks at the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/108-horror-aficionados" rel="nofollow noopener"> Horror Aficionados</a> group who have given me the the opportunity to read and discuss this and many other fine books.<br /><br /><br />Predating Dracula by 26 years, Le Fanu's novella is a classic vampire tale that gets a lot less attention than it should. It is loaded with Gothic atmosphere and also introduces a lesbian vampire theme that, while appropriately circumspect, is unmistakable and something that I never would have expected in a novella written in the 1870s.<br /><br />Bottom line: As far as vampires go, I would much rather see this underrated gem made into a movie that the ridiculous tripe that has recently been produced. No glitter, just classic Gothic horror.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6581119-char?shelf=dark-fiction">dark-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer230742609" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9464348618725003369">After my re-read of this classic, I would give Carmilla 3.5 stars. <br/><br/>I loved the atmosphere and the language, even if I thought it was a bit too flowery at times. <br/><br/>I know that it's wrong to judge a work of this age by today's standards, but man, everyone in this book seemed stupid and too naive to be believable. The whole time, I was thinking "My God, man, wake up!"<br/><br/>I'm glad I re-read this one but I think that shall be it for me with Carmilla. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2899905703" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2899905703" />
    <a title="✨Sumi&#39;s Books✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62203305-sumi-s-books"><img alt="✨Sumi&#39;s Books✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580352861p2/62203305.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2899905703?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨Sumi&#39;s Books✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨Sumi&#39;s Books✨" href="/user/show/62203305-sumi-s-books">✨Sumi&#39;s Books✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2899905703" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10449959271838542136">Before Dracula there was Carmilla!<br/>Originally published in 1872, Dracula in 1897, this chronicles the story of a young woman's susceptibility to another seemingly young woman's (Carmilla) affections. But something is very wrong and has been wrong ever since Carmilla came into the picture. Can they stop this evil before it goes too far?<br/>This is complete and utter speculation but I just want to put it out there... this could very well be the novel that Bram Stoker read that indeed inspired him to wr</span>
  <span id="freeText10449959271838542136" style="display:none">Before Dracula there was Carmilla!<br />Originally published in 1872, Dracula in 1897, this chronicles the story of a young woman's susceptibility to another seemingly young woman's (Carmilla) affections. But something is very wrong and has been wrong ever since Carmilla came into the picture. Can they stop this evil before it goes too far?<br />This is complete and utter speculation but I just want to put it out there... this could very well be the novel that Bram Stoker read that indeed inspired him to write the novel Dracula. This novel together with Bram Stoker's Irish heritage and folklore would indeed come together beautifully to create the novel that we all know and love.<br />But enough about Dracula. Let's talk about Carmilla! I think it's absolutely fabulous that the very first vampire ever to grace the publishing world was indeed a female. Personally I found her word usage and talk of everlasting love to be so seductive that I damn near threw my arms around her in submittance. <br />I always find it very interesting when the author of a certain sex decides to write from the point of view of the opposite sex. We find that here as the author who wrote the novel was a man and is writing from the point of view of Laura who was the victim in this tragic tale of vampirism. Nevertheless, Le Fanu pulls it off with flying colors! You really do feel as if you are reading the words of a distraught woman penning the details of a horrific occurrence.<br />Although this novel held no secrets or mystery for me (the ever-faithful horror fanatic) it is indeed nothing less than a heart pounding page turner. This one had my heart racing and me reading through the pages as fast as I could to find out what happens next. This is a very well done novel and I can't quite understand why it hasn't gotten the praise that it deserves over the years... or should I say decades now?<br />This is one that every true horror fan should read! Most definitely recommend! 🖤❤️🖤</span>
  <a data-text-id="10449959271838542136" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3398125811" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3398125811" />
    <a title="Grace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34465556-grace"><img alt="Grace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588296669p2/34465556.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3398125811?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grace" href="/user/show/34465556-grace">Grace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34465556-grace?shelf=pub-1800s">pub-1800s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34465556-grace?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34465556-grace?shelf=read-2020">read-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34465556-grace?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34465556-grace?shelf=r-horrorlit-bingo-2020">r-horrorlit-bingo-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34465556-grace?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34465556-grace?shelf=owned-ebook">owned-ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34465556-grace?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3398125811" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17296588661688088714"><i>Carmilla</i> was actually written prior to and was an inspiration for Bram Stoker’s <i>Dracula</i>. That was how I first heard about this novella. I read the Wikipedia article about it and found many of the details fascinating—the evil vampire is female, and has the ability to turn into a cat. So, I decided to pick this up and read it before digging in to <i>Dracula</i>, and also just because I’m a sucker for vampire fiction. <br/><br/><b>Actual Rating: 4.2</b><br/><br/>This went by surprisingly quickly. I think that’s partially because of</span>
  <span id="freeText17296588661688088714" style="display:none"><i>Carmilla</i> was actually written prior to and was an inspiration for Bram Stoker’s <i>Dracula</i>. That was how I first heard about this novella. I read the Wikipedia article about it and found many of the details fascinating—the evil vampire is female, and has the ability to turn into a cat. So, I decided to pick this up and read it before digging in to <i>Dracula</i>, and also just because I’m a sucker for vampire fiction. <br /><br /><b>Actual Rating: 4.2</b><br /><br />This went by surprisingly quickly. I think that’s partially because of its length and the fact that I didn’t realize it was so short and partially because there was never a dull moment. There was simply no time to get bored. <br /><br />Due to the length of the novella, there wasn’t much time to have a large cast of characters. Instead, Le Fanu focuses on developing those that are present—namely, Laura, Laura’s father, and Carmilla herself. I felt like this was done well, but there was a little something lacking. I suspect this is because there are social cues and circumstances that I’m not picking up on since this was written in the nineteenth century. The writing style itself, however, was perfectly fine. <br /><br />My only regret is that I would have liked to learn a little bit more about vampires. Or, perhaps more specific information about what we are told. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>”Love will have it’s sacrifices. No sacrifice without blood.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Regardless, <i>Carmilla</i> is a must-read for anyone who loves vampires—especially anyone who loves reading about them as much as I do.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17296588661688088714" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
