<div id="review_1617930226" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1617930226" />
    <a title="Tom Lewis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41086818-tom-lewis"><img alt="Tom Lewis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1428092317p2/41086818.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1617930226?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tom Lewis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tom Lewis" href="/user/show/41086818-tom-lewis">Tom Lewis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1617930226" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9052996542364031407">“But to die as lovers may - to die together, so that they may live together.”<br/><br/>Okay, how many vampire books have you read that contain that kind of elegant prose. Carmilla is a novella that was written in 1872, so it pre-dates Dracula by about 25 years. And a lot of its influence is later seen in Dracula.<br/><br/>Being as old as it is, there’s no twists that will catch a modern reader by surprise, as pretty much every variation on the vampire genre has been played out. But what you will find is something s</span>
  <span id="freeText9052996542364031407" style="display:none">“But to die as lovers may - to die together, so that they may live together.”<br /><br />Okay, how many vampire books have you read that contain that kind of elegant prose. Carmilla is a novella that was written in 1872, so it pre-dates Dracula by about 25 years. And a lot of its influence is later seen in Dracula.<br /><br />Being as old as it is, there’s no twists that will catch a modern reader by surprise, as pretty much every variation on the vampire genre has been played out. But what you will find is something sorely lacking in modern vampire literature – a rich gothic tapestry of remote castles, and dark forests; of horse-drawn carriages, misty mountains, and superstitious peasantry; and a quiet melancholy that permeates what is at times a touching tale (with sapphic undercurrents) of a young vampire torn by the need to kill the people she loves.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9052996542364031407" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1002719819?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin">Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin</a>
      </span>

        rated it

And of course, I had to order a copy. <br/><br/>I thought it was pretty good for a short novella on vampires. It was a very different take and I did enjoy it. </span>

<div id="review_1524053379" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1524053379" />
    <a title="Brian " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30718608-brian"><img alt="Brian " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567218975p2/30718608.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1524053379?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brian " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brian " href="/user/show/30718608-brian">Brian </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1524053379" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18028212690155637063">The author takes advantage of the power of contrast. Many horror writers use contrast to throw a reader's mind off balance. Stephen King made Pennywise a joking freak of a clown, and Randal Flagg a humorous and diabolical psycho-demon. In this story, a small girl meets Carmilla, two petite and intimate little girls. The contrast twists the mind into suspended insanity when supernatural visitations come, and the small girl correlates to the events. His descriptions of vampires bring a terror seen</span>
  <span id="freeText18028212690155637063" style="display:none">The author takes advantage of the power of contrast. Many horror writers use contrast to throw a reader's mind off balance. Stephen King made Pennywise a joking freak of a clown, and Randal Flagg a humorous and diabolical psycho-demon. In this story, a small girl meets Carmilla, two petite and intimate little girls. The contrast twists the mind into suspended insanity when supernatural visitations come, and the small girl correlates to the events. His descriptions of vampires bring a terror seen in modern movies: a little girl covered in blood in a white dress of purity, a creature with no heartbeat, no breath, only a cold stare of lust and hunger. <br /><br />Half the story comes through dialogue, which I found rather confusing and crippling for the pace. Overall, the story exemplifies great writing; imagery and description fill the mind. The contrast disturbs the mind with precise clarity.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18028212690155637063" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of The Turn of the Screw</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/94602-kelly?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/94602-kelly?shelf=19th-century">19th-century</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer52281480" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5569329805746457105">An atmospheric delight, gems of beautiful images falling off the page in a simple, straightforward, and yet strangely enthralling sequence. Laced through beautifully with the Victorian obsessions of scientific inquiry and the grotesque- of its time, certainly, but beautifully explored for all that. No one does feverish obsession quite like the Victorians.<br/><br/>However, our lady narrator is dumber than Dumbo's inbred country cousin. Shame she fell victim to the narrator explains it all storytelling dev</span>
  <span id="freeText5569329805746457105" style="display:none">An atmospheric delight, gems of beautiful images falling off the page in a simple, straightforward, and yet strangely enthralling sequence. Laced through beautifully with the Victorian obsessions of scientific inquiry and the grotesque- of its time, certainly, but beautifully explored for all that. No one does feverish obsession quite like the Victorians.<br /><br />However, our lady narrator is dumber than Dumbo's inbred country cousin. Shame she fell victim to the narrator explains it all storytelling device, but yeah, just sayin'. Be warned.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1682412992639705674"> <b> Audiobook narrated by a full cast 2h 22mins 08 seconds</b><br/><br/>Audible Original selection for October<br/><br/> First published in 1872( 26 years before Bram Stoker wrote Dracula), Irish Writer Joseph Sheridan Le Fanu's Carmilla is one of the early works of vampire fiction.   <span id="freeText1682412992639705674" style="display:none"> <b> Audiobook narrated by a full cast 2h 22mins 08 seconds</b><br /><br />Audible Original selection for October<br /><br /> First published in 1872( 26 years before Bram Stoker wrote Dracula), Irish Writer Joseph Sheridan Le Fanu's Carmilla is one of the early works of vampire fiction. I think the fact that it has a female vampire as the title character is awesome. It was hard to stop listening.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('s81JfJuCuU2KqWoccAMReSNOwoNIJODD1mSsiYX9irc0NP+BMVqdOrBuMRvIEFlYXrZD9nyslTKSkQHCxeqUgQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('U44iOMPtqjDR7RPauawLS2ISNdU22T9inBMVgYSgMhjUd5TFaTWOR+sqSN0Bv0NqH+q0oAJRSpPY5rjKxLcsLg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12388666460194726938">Joseph Thomas Sheridan Le Fanu was an Irish writer of Gothic tales and mystery novels. He was the leading ghost-story writer of the nineteenth century and was central to the development of the genre in the Victorian era. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2995925.M_R__James' title='M.R. James' rel='nofollow noopener'>M.R. James</a> described Le Fanu as "absolutely in the first rank as a writer of ghost stories". Three of his best-known works are <i>Uncle Silas, Carmilla</i> and <i>The House by the Churchyar</i></span>
  <span id="freeText12388666460194726938" style="display:none">Joseph Thomas Sheridan Le Fanu was an Irish writer of Gothic tales and mystery novels. He was the leading ghost-story writer of the nineteenth century and was central to the development of the genre in the Victorian era. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2995925.M_R__James" title="M.R. James" rel="nofollow noopener">M.R. James</a> described Le Fanu as "absolutely in the first rank as a writer of ghost stories". Three of his best-known works are <i>Uncle Silas, Carmilla</i> and <i>The House by the Churchyard</i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12388666460194726938" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/47015-carmilla">Quotes from Carmilla</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;You will think me cruel, very selfish, but love is always selfish; the more ardent the more selfish. How jealous I am you cannot know. You must come with me, loving me, to death; or else hate me, and still come with me, and <i>hating</i> me through death and after. There is no such word as indifference in my apathetic nature.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/178204-you-will-think-me-cruel-very-selfish-but-love-is">254 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;For some nights I slept profoundly; but still every morning I felt the same lassitude, and a languor weighed upon me all day. I felt myself a changed girl. A strange melancholy was stealing over me, a melancholy that I would not have interrupted. Dim thoughts of death began to open, and an idea that I was slowly sinking took gentle, and, somehow, not unwelcome possession of me. If it was sad, the tone of mind which this induced was also sweet. Whatever it might be, my soul acquiesced in it.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/248842-for-some-nights-i-slept-profoundly-but-still-every-morning">203 likes</a>
